                10.1016/j.mattod.2018.03.004</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D21%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D960-973%26journal%3DMater.%2BToday%26author%3DF.%2BWu%26author%3DC.%2BZhao%26author%3DS.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BLu%26author%3DY.%2BHou%26author%3DY.%2BS.%2BHu%26author%3DJ.%2BMaier%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26title%3DMulti-electron%2Breaction%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium-based%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.mattod.2018.03.004&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03525&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.mattod.2018.03.004&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multi-electron reaction materials for sodium-based batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Feixiang; Zhao, Chenglong; Chen, Shuangqiang; Lu, Yaxiang; Hou, Yanglong; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">960-973</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MTOUAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1369-7021</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-based rechargeable batteries are very promising energy storage and conversion systems owing to their wide availability and the low cost of Na resources, which is beneficial to large-scale elec. energy storage applications in future.  In the context of attempting to achieve high-energy densities and low cost, multi-electron reaction materials for both cathodes and anodes are attracting significant attention due to high specific capacities involved.  Here, we present a brief review on recently reported multi-electron reaction materials for sodium-based batteries.  We mostly conc. on true multi-electron reactions that involve individually valence changes greater than one per redox center, but in addn. include materials in the discussion, which undergo multi-electron processes per formula unit.  The theor. gravimetric and volumetric (expanded state) capacities are studied for a broad range of examples.  Then, the practically achievable volumetric energy d. and specific energy of Na cells with hard carbon, sodium (Na), and phosphorus (P) anodes are compared.  For this purpose, various data are recalcd. and referred to the same basis cell.  The results show the potential superiority of the cells using multi-electron reaction materials and provide an intuitive understanding of the practically achievable energy densities in future Na-based rechargeable batteries.  However, these multi-electron reaction materials are facing several key challenges, which are preventing their high-performance in current cells.  In order to overcome them, general strategies from particle design to electrolyte modification are reviewed and several examples in both cathode and anode materials using such strategies are studied.  Finally, future trends and perspectives for achieving promising Na-based batteries with better performance are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2LxtInWRxRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMGj2ajE7r7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXlt1SitbY%253D&amp;md5=8a71e5960456bc6a1cee2304a1af47aa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA08472A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.                 10.1039/C6TA08472A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D18278%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DS.%2BN.%2BLiu%26author%3DZ.%2BY.%2BCai%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DA.%2BQ.%2BPan%26author%3DS.%2BQ.%2BLiang%26title%3DNitrogen-doped%2BTiO2%2Bnanospheres%2Bfor%2Badvanced%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbattery%2Band%2Bsodium-ion%2Bcapacitor%2Bapplications%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC6TA08472A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03525&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC6TA08472A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped TiO2 nanospheres for advanced sodium-ion battery and sodium-ion capacitor applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Sainan; Cai, Zhenyang; Zhou, Jiang; Pan, Anqiang; Liang, Shuquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18278-18283</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (NIBs) and sodium-ion capacitors (NICs) are considered to be promising energy storage systems for applications in future hybrid elec. vehicles (HEVs) and elec. vehicles (EVs) because of the low cost and abundance of Na.  Herein, NIBs and NICs based on nitrogen-doped TiO2 (referred to as N-TiO2) nanospheres as anode materials were analyzed.  The N-TiO2 nanospheres exhibited a stable capacity of 162 mA h g-1 over 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1, as well as a superior rate performance in NIBs.  In NICs, the N-TiO2//AC device displayed a high energy d. of ∼80.3 W h kg-1, a high power d. of ∼12 500 W kg-1, and excellent long-term cycling stability for up to 6500 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqgGvDL1Qio7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMGj2ajE7r7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslGgtbjM&amp;md5=7f557ecd6ecf68e51d96a89a17421715</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c10506"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, W.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual Doping of Titania for Enhanced Na Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Meng, Weijia; Han, Jun; Dang, Zhenzhen; Li, Diansen; Jiang, Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">37</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">44214-44223</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sluggish sodium-ion diffusion kinetics and low electronic cond. have severely restricted the development of the TiO2 anode for sodium-ion batteries.  Defect engineering, such as single-heteroatom doping and oxygen vacancies, has proven to be effective methods to improve the cond. of TiO2, but a comprehensive understanding of the synergistic effect of dual-heteroatom doping and oxygen vacancies on the sodium storage performance of TiO2 is still lacking.  Herein, we design a synergistic strategy of dual doping via the in situ doping and hydrogenation treatment to improve cond. and cycling stability of TiO2.  Expts. and theor. calcns. together revealed that N and C doping reduces the band gap of TiO2, while the presence of oxygen vacancies efficiently accelerates the diffusion of sodium ions.  Thus N, C, and oxygen vacancies with high concn. co-doped TiO2, resulting in extraordinary high-rate performance, significant stable cycling, and long-term cyclability of up to 10,000 cycles.  The synthesis strategy of dual doping proposed here emphasizes the importance of defect engineering in improving material cond. and electrode cycling stability for possible practical applications in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHMfhax5LmvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhMGj2ajE7r7Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitVaku7rO&amp;md5=e53d10d82ae4ab35690dd6e2206a153a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Z. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2201140</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/admi.202201140</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2201140%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DM.%2BL.%2BYao%26author%3DA.%2BGao%26author%3DR.%2BC.%2BChen%26author%3DQ.%2BR.%2BHe%26author%3DT.%2BH.%2BYao%26author%3DH.%2BK.%2BWang%26title%3DCore-shell%2BSe-doped%2BTiO2%2540carbon%2Bnanotubes%2Bfor%2Bhigh-performance%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadmi.202201140&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03525&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadmi.202201140&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Core-Shell Se-Doped TiO2@Carbon Nanotubes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao, Menglong; Gao, Ang; Chen, Ruochen; He, Qiangrui; Yao, Tianhao; Wang, Hongkang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2201140</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AMIDD2</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2196-7350</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Titanium dioxide (TiO2) has been considered as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), because of its abundance, safety and eco-friendliness.  However, the inferior electronic cond. and low sodium ion diffusion rate of TiO2 hinder its improvement of electrochem. performance.  To overcome these drawbacks, herein, core-shell Se-doped TiO2@carbon nanotubes (denoted as Se-TiO2@CNTs) are successfully designed and fabricated, in which the TiO2 nanoparticle aggregated shells are conformally coated on the carbon nanotubes, while the metallic Se species are phys. confined within the meso/micropores.  When examd. as a SIB anode, the Se-TiO2@CNTs electrode demonstrates excellent sodium storage performance, correspondingly delivering high reversible capacities of 222.7/208.5 mA h g-1 after 200/1000 cycles at current densities of 0.2/1.0 A g-1, and even a capacity of 140.2 mA h g-1 after 4500 cycles at a high-rate of 5.0 A g-1.  The high reversible capacity, long-term cycling stability, and high-rate capability of the Se-TiO2@CNTs can be owing to the unique structure characteristics, as the hollow/porous structure with high sp. surface area of 335.4 m2 g-1 efficiently shortens the Na+ diffusion length and facilitates the electrolyte penetration, while Se-doping and carbon supporting greatly enhance the electronic cond. of the Se-TiO2@CNTs electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjleJyfrMEMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXhnsRZyGaxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XitF2rsbrN&amp;md5=05c87d6e1533b142b48dbd4cf21b1601</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA05877B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, K. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hood, Z. D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bi, Z. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bridges, C. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">20651</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201504412"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ni, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Maier, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Self-supported nanotube arrays of sulfur-doped TiO<sub>2</sub> enabling ultrastable and robust sodium storage</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2259</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2265</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201504412</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2259-2265%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DJ.%2BNi%26author%3DS.%2BFu%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DJ.%2BMaier%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26title%3DSelf-supported%2Bnanotube%2Barrays%2Bof%2Bsulfur-doped%2BTiO2%2Benabling%2Bultrastable%2Band%2Brobust%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201504412&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03525&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201504412&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Supported Nanotube Arrays of Sulfur-Doped TiO2 Enabling Ultrastable and Robust Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Fu, Shidong; Wu, Chao; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2259-2265</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We, for the 1st time, combine the unique nanotubular architecture with high cond. by engineering self-supported nanotube arrays of S-doped TiO2 (S-TiO2).  Such doping by isovalent substitution can be helpful owing to either elastic effect or, at high enough concn., to variation of materials const. (e.g., bandgap).  S-doped TiO2 materials have been reported and characterized, yet never used as electrodes for Na-based battery behaviors.  The increase of electronic cond. could be predominately ascribed to structure affects rather than proper doping, as shown by the strong effect on the band gap.  An addnl. possibility is the introduction of an anionic deficiency (anion vacancies compensated by electron due to prepn.).  Note the deoxygenation effect of S treatment, an aliovalent effect as, e.g., achieved by donor doping TiO2, may be excluded here.  The S-TiO2 nanotube array features intrinsic merits for Na storage.  First, the self-supported nanotube array can be directly adapted for electrode without using binder and C additive.  Second, the ordered nanotube architecture exhibits large interface and channels for transfer of Na ion during cycling.  Third, the S doping drastically boosts the electron movement within the nanotubes.  Consequently, the S-TiO2 nanotubes enable superior Na storage in terms of high capacity (320 mAh/g), ultrastable cycling (91% retention over 4400 cycles), and robust rate capability (167 mAh/g at 3.35 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrObwc1x3fRibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXhnsRZyGaxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1ektbc%253D&amp;md5=cf8583f1f9e0593bbc7f6af9a5227e30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.11.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Se-hollow porous carbon composite for high-performance rechargeable K-Se batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Xianglong; Wang, Wei; Deng, Jianhua; Gao, Wei; Liu, Dingyu; Ma, Qianru; Xu, Maowen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry Frontiers</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2118-2125</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ICFNAW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2052-1553</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, a novel hollow carbon matrix was designed and prepd. using a facile NaCl crystal template for the effective encapsulation of Se.  This superior carbon electrode plays a significant role in facilitating sufficient energy storage and conversion of Se-based cathode materials.  A large sp. surface area of 416 m2 g-1 was obtained, and the matrix provided numerous hollow spheres for the storage of Se.  The thermogravimetric anal. and electrochem. results show that the as-prepd. Se-hollow porous carbon composite with an ideal Se content of 42% can make excellent capacity contribution.  The hollow porous structure not only effectively accommodates the volumetric expansion during the discharge-charge process but also makes the composite have a good contact with the electrolyte.  In addn., the 3D open framework structure can be conducive to fast electron transportation.  As a result, the Se-hollow porous carbon composite exhibited outstanding electrochem. performance when evaluated as a cathode material for rechargeable K-Se batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWKrO846Nb67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXhnsRZyGaxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1KgtrvI&amp;md5=f63b097f91c9be923d037e696a923045</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104829"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Doping is an effective strategy for tuning metal oxide-based semiconductors for solar-driven photoelectrochem. (PEC) water splitting.  Despite decades of extensive research effort, the dopant selection is still largely dependent on a trial-and-error approach.  Machine learning (ML) is promising in providing predictable insights on the dopant selection for high-performing PEC systems because it can uncover correlations from the seemingly ambiguous linkages between vast features of dopants and the PEC performance of doped photoelectrodes.  Herein, the authors successfully build ML model to predict the doping effect of 17 metal dopants into hematite (Fe2O3), a prototype photoelectrode material.  Their findings disclose the crit. parameters from the 10 intrinsic features of each dopant.  The model is further exptl. validated by the coherent prediction on Y and La dopants'behaviors.  Further interpretation of the ML model suggests that the chem. state is the most significant selection criteria, meanwhile, dopants with higher metal-oxygen bond formation enthalpy and larger ionic radius are favored in improving the charge sepn. and transfer (CST) in the Fe2O3 photoanodes.  The generic feature of this ML guided selection criteria has been further extended to CuO-based photoelectrodes showing improved CST by alk. metal ions doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp7AfkCCJeJTbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIrcVTVwzkQQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-scale battery systems are essential for efficiently utilizing renewable energy power sources from solar and wind, which can generate electricity only intermittently.  The use of lithium-ion batteries to store the generated energy is one soln.  A long cycle life is crit. for lithium-ion battery when used in these applications; this is different from portable devices which require 1,000 cycles at most.  Here we demonstrate a novel co-substituted lithium iron phosphate cathode with estd. 70%-capacity retention of 25,000 cycles.  This is found by exploring a wide chem. compositional space using d. functional theory calcns.  Relative vol. change of a compd. between fully lithiated and delithiated conditions is used as the descriptor for the cycle life.  On the basis of the results of the screening, synthesis of selected materials is targeted.  Single-phase samples with the required chem. compn. are successfully made by an epoxide-mediated sol-gel method.  The optimized materials show excellent cycle-life performance as lithium-ion battery cathodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpkar8N9MWnibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgIrcVTVwzkQQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVWgs7fK&amp;md5=4e4b3f925cf2301be57940302c7bc21f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.mattod.2023.06.013"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Satrughna, J.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into Diffusion Mechanisms in P2 Layered Oxide Materials by First-Principles Calculations</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mo, Yifei; Ong, Shyue Ping; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Significant progress was made in Na-intercalation compds. for rechargeable Na batteries.  P2 NaxMO2 layered oxides have been shown to have high capacity, good cyclability, and improved rate capability.  The authors study the diffusion mechanisms in P2 NaxCoO2 using ab initio mol. dynamics simulations and nudged elastic band calcns.  The authors identify the Na diffusion mechanisms in P2 NaxCoO2 at non-dil. Na concns. and illustrate the strong effect of Na-Na interactions on Na diffusion.                 10.1039/c1ee01782a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D3680%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DS.%2BP.%2BOng%26author%3DV.%2BL.%2BChevrier%26author%3DG.%2BHautier%26author%3DA.%2BJain%26author%3DC.%2BMoore%26author%3DS.%2BKim%26author%3DX.%2BH.%2BMa%26author%3DG.%2BCeder%26title%3DVoltage%252C%2Bstability%2Band%2Bdiffusion%2Bbarrier%2Bdifferences%2Bbetween%2Bsodium-ion%2Band%2Blithium-ion%2Bintercalation%2Bmaterials%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc1ee01782a&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03525&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc1ee01782a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ong, Shyue Ping; Chevrier, Vincent L.; Hautier, Geoffroy; Jain, Anubhav; Moore, Charles; Kim, Sangtae; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3680-3688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To evaluate the potential of Na-ion batteries, we contrast in this work the difference between Na-ion and Li-ion based intercalation chemistries in terms of three key battery properties-voltage, phase stability and diffusion barriers.  The compds. investigated comprise the layered AMO2 and AMS2 structures, the olivine and maricite AMPO4 structures, and the NASICON A3V2(PO4)3 structures.  The calcd. Na voltages for the compds. investigated are 0.18-0.57 V lower than that of the corresponding Li voltages, in agreement with previous exptl. data.  We believe the obsd. lower voltages for Na compds. are predominantly a cathodic effect related to the much smaller energy gain from inserting Na into the host structure compared to inserting Li.  We also found a relatively strong dependence of battery properties on structural features.  In general, the difference between the Na and Li voltage of the same structure, ΔVNa-Li, is less neg. for the maricite structures preferred by Na, and more neg. for the olivine structures preferred by Li.  The layered compds. have the most neg. ΔVNa-Li.  In terms of phase stability, we found that open structures, such as the layered and NASICON structures, that are better able to accommodate the larger Na+ ion generally have both Na and Li versions of the same compd.  For the close-packed AMPO4 structures, our results show that Na generally prefers the maricite structure, while Li prefers the olivine structure, in agreement with previous exptl. work.  We also found surprising evidence that the barriers for Na+ migration can potentially be lower than that for Li+ migration in the layered structures.  Overall, our findings indicate that Na-ion systems can be competitive with Li-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosFyTQ7K1B3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhk2yIVCTqgGA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1CqsLzK&amp;md5=5a6e72a3ae5ebf92d84322240b2c29cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b01989"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dacek, S.                 10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b01989</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D5450-5460%26journal%3DChem.%2BMater.%26author%3DS.%2BT.%2BDacek%26author%3DW.%2BD.%2BRichards%26author%3DD.%2BA.%2BKitchaev%26author%3DG.%2BCeder%26title%3DStructure%2Band%2Bdynamics%2Bof%2Bfluorophosphate%2BNa-ion%2Bbattery%2Bcathodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemmater.6b01989&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.4c03525&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemmater.6b01989&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure and Dynamics of Fluorophosphate Na-Ion Battery Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dacek, Stephen T.; Richards, William D.; Kitchaev, Daniil A.; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5450-5460</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fluorophosphate cathodes with the chem. formula NaxV2(PO4)2O2yF3-2y (0 ≤ x ≤ 4, 0 ≤ y ≤ 1) are some of the few known sodium-ion cathode materials with the potential to be competitive with conventional lithium-ion cathodes.  However, the exptl. accessible performance of the fluorophosphates remains limited, primarily due to the fact that only half of the theor. capacity has been reversibly cycled.  In this article, we review the extensive body of literature on the fluorophosphate class of sodium-ion cathodes and, in combination with our own ab initio model of the material, investigate the mechanisms underlying the sodium-extn. limitations in the NaxV2(PO4)2F3 (y = 0) fluorophosphate.  Specifically, we focus on the potential to reversibly ext. sodium beyond the 1 ≤ x ≤ 3 range.  We find that this limitation arises from a combination of the high voltage of the V4+/5+ oxidn. reaction assocd. with sodium extn. in the 0 ≤ x ≤ 1 region and a precipitous drop in sodium diffusivity near the x = 1 compn. due to the presence of a strong ordering, which prevents the formation of mobile defects in the structure.  We conclude that the accessible capacity of NaxV2(PO4)2F3 can potentially be expanded to 0 ≤ x ≤ 3 by introducing defects into the material and reducing the voltage of the transition metal redox couple, both of which can likely be achieved via transition metal substitution and aliovalent anion doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3YGS0IXn6K7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhk2yIVCTqgGA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFKrt7rP&amp;md5=1817ec5d2300e2baca0449bbc321936d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702998"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and fluorine co-doped TiO2/carbon microspheres for advanced anodes in sodium-ion batteries: High volumetric capacity, superior power density and large areal capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lv, Dan; Wang, Dongdong; Wang, Nana; Liu, Hongxia; Zhang, Shaojie; Zhu, Yansong; Song, Kepeng; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">68</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104-112</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Fast charging and high volumetric capacity are two of the crit. demands for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Although nanostructured materials achieve outstanding rate performance, they suffer from low tap d. and small volumetric capacity.  Therefore, how to realize large volumetric capacity and high tap d. simultaneously is very challenging.  Here, N/F co-doped TiO2/carbon microspheres (NF-TiO2/C) are synthesized to achieve both of them.  Theor. calcns. reveal that N and F co-doping increases the contents of oxygen vacancies and narrows the bandgaps of TiO2 and C, improving the electronic cond. of NF-TiO2/C.  Furthermore, NF-TiO2/C exhibits the high binding energy and low diffusion energy barrier of Na+, significantly facilitating Na+ storage and Na+ diffusion.  Therefore, NF-TiO2/C offers a high tap d. (1.51 g cm-3), an outstanding rate performance (∼125.9 mAh g-1 at 100 C), a large volumetric capacity (∼190 mAh cm-3 at 100 C), a high areal capacity (∼4.8 mAh cm-2) and an ultra-long cycling performance (∼80.2% after 10,000 cycles at 10 C) simultaneously.  In addn., NF-TiO2/C||Na3V2(PO4)3 full cells achieve an ultrahigh power d. of 25.2 kW kg-1.  These results indicate the great promise of NF-TiO2/C as a high-volumetric-capacity and high-power-d. anode material of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrHVu7UjTFaQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhk2yIVCTqgGA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFOju7jM&amp;md5=c3571797aa78b29e05d08e8a4409d6dc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.3390/molecules22030414"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gurkan, Y.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced photocatalytic activity of Se-doped TiO2 under visible light irradiation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie Wei; Li Rui; Xu Qingyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Anatase TiO2 is a typical photocatalyst, and its excellent performance is limited in ultraviolet light range due to its wide band gap of 3.2 eV.  A series of Se-doped TiO2 nanoparticles in anatase structure with various Se concentrations up to 17.1 at.% were prepared using sol-gel method.  The doped Se ions are confirmed to be mainly in the valence state of + 4, which provides extra electronic states in the band gap of TiO2.  The band gap is effectively narrowed with the smallest gap energy of 2.17 eV, and the photocatalytic activity is effectively improved due to the extended absorption range.  The photocatalytic activity was evaluated by the degradation of Rhodamine B (RhB) in aqueous solution under visible light irradiation.  The results show that Se doping significantly improves the photocatalytic activity of TiO2 and 13.63 at.% Se-doped TiO2 has the best performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTZUVp89Gd1ZjAyhZbj3lKdfW6udTcc2eZQjQTp46j39bntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC1MblsFKlug%253D%253D&amp;md5=70cd9ce2308d5bacc58cb5ca0025e4f6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202211661"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Q. (E) Rate performances of the TiO<sub>2</sub>, N-TiO<sub>2</sub>, Se-TiO<sub>2</sub>, and N, Se-TiO<sub>2</sub>-1/3 electrodes ramping from 0.1 to 20 A g<sup>–1</sup> and back to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (F) Cycling stabilities of the four electrodes during 5000 cycles at 2.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>. (G) Cycling stabilities of the TiO<sub>2</sub> and N, Se-TiO<sub>2</sub>-1/3 electrodes over 10,000 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Dynamic analyses of the dual-doped TiO<sub>2</sub> electrode. (A) GITT profiles. (B) Diffusion coefficients calculated from GITT profiles as a function of potential for TiO<sub>2</sub>, N-TiO<sub>2</sub>, Se-TiO<sub>2</sub>, and N, Se-TiO<sub>2</sub>-1/3. (C) CV curves at various scan rates from 0.2 to 10 mV s<sup>–1</sup> for N, Se-TiO<sub>2</sub>-1/3. (D) Analysis of <i>b</i> values using the relationship between peak current and scan rate. (E) Contribution ratio of the capacitive- and diffusion-controlled charge versus scan rate.                         rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Defect-assisted selective surface phosphorus doping to enhance rate capability of titanium dioxide for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Qingmeng; He, Hanna; Zhu, Youhuan; Wang, Zhenyu; Qin, Ning; Gu, Shuai; Li, Zhiqiang; Luo, Wen; Lu, Zhouguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9247-9258</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phosphorus doping is an effective strategy to simultaneously improve the electronic cond. and regulate the ionic diffusion kinetics of TiO2 being considered as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  However, efficient phosphorus doping at high concn. in well-crystd. TiO2 nanoparticles is still a big challenge.  Herein, the authors propose a defect-assisted phosphorus doping strategy to selectively engineer the surface structure of TiO2 nanoparticles.  The reduced TiO2-x shell layer that is rich in oxygen defects and Ti3+ species precisely triggered a high concn. of phosphorus doping (∼7.8 at.%), and consequently a TiO2@TiO2-x-P core@shell architecture was produced.  Comprehensive characterizations and first-principle calcns. proved that the surface-functionalized TiO2-x-P thin layer endowed the TiO2@TiO2-x-P with substantially enhanced electronic cond. and accelerated Na ion transportation, resulting in great rate capability (167 mA h g-1 at 10 000 mA g-1) and stable cycling (99% after 5000 cycles at 10 A g-1).  Combining in/ex situ x-ray diffraction with ex situ ESR clearly demonstrated the high reversibility and robust mech. behavior of TiO2@TiO2-x-P upon long-term cycling.  This work provides an interesting and effective strategy for precise heteroatoms doping to improve the electrochem. performance of nanoparticles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoV2X3aWTMl9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljGjAjfZk06ZQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsVamtb7P&amp;md5=cd8e232f3259e7881601dbcf23b2e6ee</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2022.03.043"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y. K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion batteries: Present and future</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3614</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljGjAjfZk06ZQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202304251"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbon has been regarded as the most promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its low cost, high reversible capacity, and low working potential.  However, the uncertain sodium storage mechanism hinders the rational design and synthesis of high-performance hard carbon anode materials for practical SIBs.  During the past decades, tremendous efforts have been put to stimulate the development of hard carbon materials.  In this review, we discuss the recent progress of the study on the sodium storage mechanism of hard carbon anodes, and the effective strategies to improve their sodium storage performance have been summarized.  It is anticipated that hard carbon anodes with high electrochem. properties will be inspired and fabricated for large-scale energy storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJBzNU_bMKCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lix_qxHRWDXNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhsVGgsL%252FJ&amp;md5=7990adfff3d72f282da700e66ef36276</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1039/D3EE01154B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.                         rightTab-cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multi-electron reaction materials for sodium-based batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Feixiang; Zhao, Chenglong; Chen, Shuangqiang; Lu, Yaxiang; Hou, Yanglong; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Sodium-based rechargeable batteries are very promising energy storage and conversion systems owing to their wide availability and the low cost of Na resources, which is beneficial to large-scale elec. energy storage applications in future.  In the context of attempting to achieve high-energy densities and low cost, multi-electron reaction materials for both cathodes and anodes are attracting significant attention due to high specific capacities involved.  Here, we present a brief review on recently reported multi-electron reaction materials for sodium-based batteries.  We mostly conc. on true multi-electron reactions that involve individually valence changes greater than one per redox center, but in addn. include materials in the discussion, which undergo multi-electron processes per formula unit.  The theor. gravimetric and volumetric (expanded state) capacities are studied for a broad range of examples.  Then, the practically achievable volumetric energy d. and specific energy of Na cells with hard carbon, sodium (Na), and phosphorus (P) anodes are compared.  For this purpose, various data are recalcd. and referred to the same basis cell.  The results show the potential superiority of the cells using multi-electron reaction materials and provide an intuitive understanding of the practically achievable energy densities in future Na-based rechargeable batteries.  However, these multi-electron reaction materials are facing several key challenges, which are preventing their high-performance in current cells.  In order to overcome them, general strategies from particle design to electrolyte modification are reviewed and several examples in both cathode and anode materials using such strategies are studied.  Finally, future trends and perspectives for achieving promising Na-based batteries with better performance are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2LxtInWRxRbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lix_qxHRWDXNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXlt1SitbY%253D&amp;md5=8a71e5960456bc6a1cee2304a1af47aa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA08472A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The sluggish sodium-ion diffusion kinetics and low electronic cond. have severely restricted the development of the TiO2 anode for sodium-ion batteries.  Defect engineering, such as single-heteroatom doping and oxygen vacancies, has proven to be effective methods to improve the cond. of TiO2, but a comprehensive understanding of the synergistic effect of dual-heteroatom doping and oxygen vacancies on the sodium storage performance of TiO2 is still lacking.  Herein, we design a synergistic strategy of dual doping via the in situ doping and hydrogenation treatment to improve cond. and cycling stability of TiO2.  Expts. and theor. calcns. together revealed that N and C doping reduces the band gap of TiO2, while the presence of oxygen vacancies efficiently accelerates the diffusion of sodium ions.  Thus N, C, and oxygen vacancies with high concn. co-doped TiO2, resulting in extraordinary high-rate performance, significant stable cycling, and long-term cyclability of up to 10,000 cycles.  The synthesis strategy of dual doping proposed here emphasizes the importance of defect engineering in improving material cond. and electrode cycling stability for possible practical applications in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoHMfhax5LmvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lix_qxHRWDXNg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXitVaku7rO&amp;md5=e53d10d82ae4ab35690dd6e2206a153a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Z.                         rightTab-cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Core-Shell Se-Doped TiO2@Carbon Nanotubes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yao, Menglong; Gao, Ang; Chen, Ruochen; He, Qiangrui; Yao, Tianhao; Wang, Hongkang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2201140</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Titanium dioxide (TiO2) has been considered as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), because of its abundance, safety and eco-friendliness.  However, the inferior electronic cond. and low sodium ion diffusion rate of TiO2 hinder its improvement of electrochem. performance.  To overcome these drawbacks, herein, core-shell Se-doped TiO2@carbon nanotubes (denoted as Se-TiO2@CNTs) are successfully designed and fabricated, in which the TiO2 nanoparticle aggregated shells are conformally coated on the carbon nanotubes, while the metallic Se species are phys. confined within the meso/micropores.  When examd. as a SIB anode, the Se-TiO2@CNTs electrode demonstrates excellent sodium storage performance, correspondingly delivering high reversible capacities of 222.7/208.5 mA h g-1 after 200/1000 cycles at current densities of 0.2/1.0 A g-1, and even a capacity of 140.2 mA h g-1 after 4500 cycles at a high-rate of 5.0 A g-1.  The high reversible capacity, long-term cycling stability, and high-rate capability of the Se-TiO2@CNTs can be owing to the unique structure characteristics, as the hollow/porous structure with high sp. surface area of 335.4 m2 g-1 efficiently shortens the Na+ diffusion length and facilitates the electrolyte penetration, while Se-doping and carbon supporting greatly enhance the electronic cond. of the Se-TiO2@CNTs electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjleJyfrMEMLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0likTrSsUKLBBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XitF2rsbrN&amp;md5=05c87d6e1533b142b48dbd4cf21b1601</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA05877B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.                 10.1002/adma.201504412</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Supported Nanotube Arrays of Sulfur-Doped TiO2 Enabling Ultrastable and Robust Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Fu, Shidong; Wu, Chao; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2259-2265</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We, for the 1st time, combine the unique nanotubular architecture with high cond. by engineering self-supported nanotube arrays of S-doped TiO2 (S-TiO2).  Such doping by isovalent substitution can be helpful owing to either elastic effect or, at high enough concn., to variation of materials const. (e.g., bandgap).  S-doped TiO2 materials have been reported and characterized, yet never used as electrodes for Na-based battery behaviors.  The increase of electronic cond. could be predominately ascribed to structure affects rather than proper doping, as shown by the strong effect on the band gap.  An addnl. possibility is the introduction of an anionic deficiency (anion vacancies compensated by electron due to prepn.).  Note the deoxygenation effect of S treatment, an aliovalent effect as, e.g., achieved by donor doping TiO2, may be excluded here.  The S-TiO2 nanotube array features intrinsic merits for Na storage.  First, the self-supported nanotube array can be directly adapted for electrode without using binder and C additive.  Second, the ordered nanotube architecture exhibits large interface and channels for transfer of Na ion during cycling.  Third, the S doping drastically boosts the electron movement within the nanotubes.  Consequently, the S-TiO2 nanotubes enable superior Na storage in terms of high capacity (320 mAh/g), ultrastable cycling (91% retention over 4400 cycles), and robust rate capability (167 mAh/g at 3.35 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrObwc1x3fRibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0likTrSsUKLBBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1ektbc%253D&amp;md5=cf8583f1f9e0593bbc7f6af9a5227e30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.11.008"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Se-hollow porous carbon composite for high-performance rechargeable K-Se batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Xianglong; Wang, Wei; Deng, Jianhua; Gao, Wei; Liu, Dingyu; Ma, Qianru; Xu, Maowen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry Frontiers</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, a novel hollow carbon matrix was designed and prepd. using a facile NaCl crystal template for the effective encapsulation of Se.  This superior carbon electrode plays a significant role in facilitating sufficient energy storage and conversion of Se-based cathode materials. The thermogravimetric anal. and electrochem. results show that the as-prepd. Se-hollow porous carbon composite with an ideal Se content of 42% can make excellent capacity contribution.                         rightTab-cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ong, Shyue Ping; Chevrier, Vincent L.; Hautier, Geoffroy; Jain, Anubhav; Moore, Charles; Kim, Sangtae; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To evaluate the potential of Na-ion batteries, we contrast in this work the difference between Na-ion and Li-ion based intercalation chemistries in terms of three key battery properties-voltage, phase stability and diffusion barriers.  The compds. investigated comprise the layered AMO2 and AMS2 structures, the olivine and maricite AMPO4 structures, and the NASICON A3V2(PO4)3 structures.  The calcd. Na voltages for the compds. investigated are 0.18-0.57 V lower than that of the corresponding Li voltages, in agreement with previous exptl. data.  We believe the obsd. lower voltages for Na compds. are predominantly a cathodic effect related to the much smaller energy gain from inserting Na into the host structure compared to inserting Li.  We also found a relatively strong dependence of battery properties on structural features.  In general, the difference between the Na and Li voltage of the same structure, ΔVNa-Li, is less neg. for the maricite structures preferred by Na, and more neg. for the olivine structures preferred by Li.  The layered compds. have the most neg. ΔVNa-Li.  In terms of phase stability, we found that open structures, such as the layered and NASICON structures, that are better able to accommodate the larger Na+ ion generally have both Na and Li versions of the same compd.  For the close-packed AMPO4 structures, our results show that Na generally prefers the maricite structure, while Li prefers the olivine structure, in agreement with previous exptl. work.  We also found surprising evidence that the barriers for Na+ migration can potentially be lower than that for Li+ migration in the layered structures.  Overall, our findings indicate that Na-ion systems can be competitive with Li-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosFyTQ7K1B3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljn2avaq3LtDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1CqsLzK&amp;md5=5a6e72a3ae5ebf92d84322240b2c29cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b01989"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dacek, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Fluorophosphate cathodes with the chem. formula NaxV2(PO4)2O2yF3-2y (0 ≤ x ≤ 4, 0 ≤ y ≤ 1) are some of the few known sodium-ion cathode materials with the potential to be competitive with conventional lithium-ion cathodes.  However, the exptl. accessible performance of the fluorophosphates remains limited, primarily due to the fact that only half of the theor. capacity has been reversibly cycled.  In this article, we review the extensive body of literature on the fluorophosphate class of sodium-ion cathodes and, in combination with our own ab initio model of the material, investigate the mechanisms underlying the sodium-extn. limitations in the NaxV2(PO4)2F3 (y = 0) fluorophosphate.  Specifically, we focus on the potential to reversibly ext. sodium beyond the 1 ≤ x ≤ 3 range.  We find that this limitation arises from a combination of the high voltage of the V4+/5+ oxidn. reaction assocd. with sodium extn. in the 0 ≤ x ≤ 1 region and a precipitous drop in sodium diffusivity near the x = 1 compn. due to the presence of a strong ordering, which prevents the formation of mobile defects in the structure.  We conclude that the accessible capacity of NaxV2(PO4)2F3 can potentially be expanded to 0 ≤ x ≤ 3 by introducing defects into the material and reducing the voltage of the transition metal redox couple, both of which can likely be achieved via transition metal substitution and aliovalent anion doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr3YGS0IXn6K7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljn2avaq3LtDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtFKrt7rP&amp;md5=1817ec5d2300e2baca0449bbc321936d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref39" class="rightTabRefNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit39" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702998"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.
